## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics (continuous-time growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, which is the standard state variable in continuous population dynamics. Typical relationships express per-capita growth as a function of density (P) and/or time-varying environment (t), including density dependence, Allee effects, harvesting, and seasonal forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Linear birth–death with immigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net proportional growth plus constant influx)
- Density-dependent (quadratic) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth when c1 < 0)
- Time-varying intrinsic rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (gradually improving/worsening environment)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting reproduction/survival)
- Gompertz growth (log-density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth decreases with log(P))
- Theta-logistic (generalized logistic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (P / c1)**c2) (flexible density dependence curvature)
- Richards growth (generalized sigmoid): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (P / c1)**c2) * (P / c1)**c3 (adds asymmetry via extra power term)
- Allee effect (strong Allee): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - P / c2) (growth negative below threshold c1, limited by carrying capacity c2)
- Weak Allee (reduced growth at low density): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) * (P / (P + c2)) (low-density suppression without negative growth necessarily)
- Harvesting (constant yield): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) - c2 (constant removal; possible extinction threshold)
- Harvesting (proportional): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) - c2 * P (effort proportional to population)
- Saturating harvest (Holling type II removal): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (limited catch/consumption at high P)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth analysis: rewriting as (dP_dt)/P = g(t, P) often reveals whether density dependence is linear in P, log(P), or a higher-order power.
- Carrying capacity behavior: factors like (1 - P/c1) or log(c1/P) imply dP_dt → 0 as P → c1, indicating an equilibrium near c1.
- Crowding strength/shape: replacing (1 - P/c1) by (1 - (P/c1)**c2) changes how sharply growth slows near capacity (c2 > 1 sharper; 0 < c2 < 1 softer).
- Allee thresholds: inclusion of (P - c1) (or equivalent) introduces an unstable equilibrium at P = c1, separating extinction vs persistence regimes.
- Harvest signatures: subtracting c2 (constant yield) can create a critical population below which recovery is impossible; subtracting c2 * P shifts the effective intrinsic growth rate.
- Seasonality/time forcing: sinusoidal terms in coefficients of P indicate periodic modulation of birth/death rates; may produce oscillatory transients around equilibria even without predator-prey states.
- Finite-time blow-up avoidance: biologically plausible models typically make dP_dt sub-quadratic for large P (or enforce negative feedback) to prevent unrealistic super-exponential growth.
- Equilibria from factorization: expressions that factor into P * f(P) make equilibria explicit at P = 0 and roots of f(P), aiding interpretation and regression regularization.

GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P**c4 + c5*P*exp(-c6*t)
Candidate formulas: 51

GT (fixed):
\[
0.712449\,P - \frac{0.712449}{68.906009}P^2 \;+\; 0.712449\,P^{1/3}\;+\;0.712449\,P\,e^{-0.03459336\,t}.
\]
So GT is exactly a sum of four independent basis terms: \(P^{1/3}\), \(P\), \(P^2\), and \(P e^{kt}\) with \(k<0\). No other \(P\)-dependence (logs, rationals like \(1/(P+c)\), trig, max, etc.) can appear unless its coefficient is set to 0.

Below, for each candidate, I check whether it can be reduced (by choosing constants) to exactly those four terms and nothing else.

1) \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^{1/3}c1\log(Pc2+1)\cos(c3 t)+ P^2c4 + Pc5 + Pc6e^{c7 t}\).
- Set \(c1=0\) to remove the log*cos term.
- Choose \(c0=0.712449\), \(c4=-0.712449/68.906009\), \(c5=0.712449\), \(c6=0.712449\), \(c7=-0.03459336\).
- Matches GT.

2) \(P^{1/3}c0 + \frac{P^3 c1}{P+c2} + P^2c3 + \frac{P^2 c4}{P+c2} + Pc5 + Pc6e^{c7 t}\).
- Terms with \((P+c2)^{-1}\) are non-polynomial in \(P\); GT has none. Only way: set \(c1=0\) and \(c4=0\).
- Then it becomes \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c3 + Pc5 + Pc6e^{c7 t}\), which can match GT by choosing constants as in (1) (with \(c3\) as the quadratic coefficient).
- Matches GT.

3) Same as (2) but includes extra \(Pc6\) and \(Pc7e^{c8 t}\).
- Set rational terms off: \(c1=0,c4=0\).
- Then \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c3 + P(c5+c6) + Pc7e^{c8 t}\). Choose \(c5+c6=0.712449\), \(c0=0.712449\), \(c3=-0.712449/68.906009\), \(c7=0.712449\), \(c8=-0.03459336\).
- Matches GT.

4) \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\log(1+c3/P)+ Pc4e^{c5 t}+ Pc6 + P^{c7}c8\).
- GT needs \(P^{1/3}\) and \(P e^{kt}\). Here exponential term is \(P e^{c5 t}\) (good), but there is no \(P^{1/3}\) unless \(P^{c7}c8\) is used with \(c7=1/3\).
- However there is an extra \(Pc6\) (can merge into \(Pc1\)) and the log term must be removed: set \(c2=0\).
- Then choose \(c8=0.712449, c7=1/3\); \(c0=-0.712449/68.906009\); \(c1+c6=0.712449\); \(c4=0.712449\); \(c5=-0.03459336\).
- Matches GT.

5) \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + Pc3 + Pc4e^{c5 t} + Pc6\log(1+c7/P)\).
- Remove log: \(c6=0\).
- Combine linear terms: \(P(c2+c3)\).
- Choose \(c0=0.712449\), \(c1=-0.712449/68.906009\), \(c2+c3=0.712449\), \(c4=0.712449\), \(c5=-0.03459336\).
- Matches GT.

6) \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^3c1 + P^2c2 + P^2c3 + P^2c4 + Pc5 + Pc6 + Pc7 + Pc8e^{c9 t}\).
- GT has no \(P^3\): set \(c1=0\).
- Quadratic coefficient is \(c2+c3+c4\); linear is \(c5+c6+c7\).
- Choose \(c0=0.712449\), \(c2+c3+c4=-0.712449/68.906009\), \(c5+c6+c7=0.712449\), \(c8=0.712449\), \(c9=-0.03459336\).

7) \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + P c2 (Pc3)^{c4}(Pc3)^{c5} + Pc6 + Pc7e^{c8 t} + P c9 (Pc3)^{c5}\).
- The power terms create \(P^{1+c4+c5}\) and \(P^{1+c5}\) (times constants). GT only allows \(P\) and \(P^2\) besides \(P^{1/3}\).
- You could try to set these coefficients to 0: set \(c2=0\) and \(c9=0\), eliminating both power-generated terms.

- Matches GT.

- Then linear terms combine: \(P(c5+c6+c9)\).

The power term is \(P^{1+c4}\), which cannot be \(P^{1/3}\) because it is multiplied by an extra leading \(P\) (so exponent is \(1+c4\)); setting \(1+c4=1/3\) gives \(c4=-2/3\), but then the term is \(P^{1/3}\) indeed (since \(P\cdot P^{c4}=P^{1+c4}\)). However it also includes \((c3)^{c4}\) constant factor, which is fine.
- But then you still need a linear \(P\) term and a quadratic \(P^2\) term and \(P e^{kt}\). Those are available via \(Pc1+Pc7\), \(P^2c0\), and \(Pc5e^{c6 t}\).
- So set \(c4=-2/3\) and choose \(c2(c3)^{c4}=0.712449\) to match the \(P^{1/3}\) coefficient; set \(c0=-0.712449/68.906009\); set \(c1+c7=0.712449\); set \(c5=0.712449\), \(c6=-0.03459336\).

You can zero out the non-GT parts by setting \(c0=c2=c4=0\) (kills rationals), \(c5=0\) (kills log), and use \(P^{c8}c9\) to create \(P^{1/3}\) (set \(c8=1/3,c9=0.712449\)), keep \(Pc3\) for linear, and \(Pc6e^{c7 t}\) for exponential. - Need both a plain \(P\) and a \(P^2\) and a \(P^{1/3}\) and a single \(P e^{kt}\).
- You can set one power term to \(P^2\) (say \(c1=2\)), another to \(P^{1/3}\) (say \(c3=1/3\) but then it’s multiplied by \(e^{c5 t}\), which GT does not have), or \(c6=1/3\) but again multiplied by an exponential in \(t\).
- There is no standalone \(P^{1/3}\) without an \(e^{(\cdot)t}\) factor. Setting the exponential rate to 0 would make it time-independent, but then it becomes just another power term and you still need the actual \(P e^{kt}\) term with \(k\neq 0\).
- With only two exponential-bearing terms, you can’t simultaneously create (i) a time-independent \(P^{1/3}\) and (ii) a time-dependent \(P e^{kt}\) while also having \(P^2\) and \(P\).
- No match.

37) \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 e^{c3 t} + P^{c4}c5 e^{c6 t}\).
- No \(P^{1/3}\) term unless \(c4=1/3\) but then it is multiplied by \(e^{c6 t}\). If set \(c6=0\) to remove time dependence, then you lose the needed \(P e^{kt}\) unless \(Pc2 e^{c3 t}\) provides it (it can), but then you still need the plain linear \(P\) term (from \(Pc1\)) and quadratic (from \(P^2c0\))—those exist. So choose \(c4=1/3, c6=0\) gives standalone \(P^{1/3}\).
- Then set \(c2=0.712449, c3=-0.03459336\) for \(P e^{kt}\); set \(c1=0.712449\); set \(c0=-0.712449/68.906009\); set \(c5=0.712449\).
- Matches GT.

38) Has extra \(Pc2\log(1+c3/P)\) and extra \(P^{c6}c7 e^{c8 t}\). Set \(c2=0\) to remove log. Use \(P^{c6}c7 e^{c8 t}\) either as 0 (set \(c7=0\)) or merge with the \(P e^{kt}\) term by setting \(c6=1\) and matching \(c8\); but there is already \(Pc4e^{c5 t}\). Easiest: set \(c7=0\). Then it lacks \(P^{1/3}\) entirely.
- So cannot match.
- No match.

39) Similar: \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2e^{c3 t} + P c4/(P+c5) + P^{c6}c7 e^{c8 t}\).
- Must remove rational: set \(c4=0\). Then still no \(P^{1/3}\) unless \(c6=1/3\), but that term has \(e^{c8 t}\). If set \(c8=0\) to make it time-independent, then you still need \(P e^{kt}\) from \(Pc2e^{c3 t}\) (ok). Then choose \(c6=1/3, c7=0.712449\), \(c2=0.712449, c3=-0.03459336\), \(c1=0.712449\), \(c0=-0.712449/68.906009\).
- Matches GT.

40) Has extra \(P c6 t\) (linear in \(t\)); GT has no such term. Must set \(c6=0\). Then reduces to (12)/(17) form and matches.
- Matches GT.

41) Has extra \(P c7 t\); must set \(c7=0\). Then matches.
- Matches GT.

42) Has extra \(c7\log(Pc8+1)\) (not multiplied by \(P\)); GT has no such term. Must set \(c7=0\). Then expression has no \(P^{1/3}\) term at all. So cannot match.
- No match.

43) Has extra \(c5\log(c6 e^{Pc7+c8 t}+1)\) (non-polynomial in \(P\)); must set \(c5=0\). Then reduces to (22) and matches.
- Matches GT.

44) Entire expression is divided by \(P+c1\) (all terms have that denominator). GT has no such global rational factor; the only way would be to make numerator equal GT*(P+c1), which would introduce \(P^{4/3}\), \(P^{7/3}\), etc. Not possible with the limited numerator structure for all \(P\). Setting coefficients to kill denominator effect can’t remove the denominator itself.
- No match.

45) Has extra oscillatory factor \(\sin(c8 t+c9)\) multiplying a \(P^{c5}e^{c7 t}\) term; GT has no sinusoid. Only way: set its coefficient \(c6=0\) (or otherwise zero the whole term). Then reduces to (22) and matches.
- Matches GT.

46) \(Pc0 + Pc1\log(c2 e^{c3 t}+1) + P^{c4}c5 + P^{c6}c7 e^{c8 t}\).
- The \(P\log(\cdot)\) term depends on \(t\) but not as a pure exponential; GT doesn’t have it. Must set \(c1=0\).
- Then use \(P^{c4}c5\) for \(P^{1/3}\) (set \(c4=1/3\)), and \(P^{c6}c7 e^{c8 t}\) for \(P e^{kt}\) (set \(c6=1\)).
- But there is no \(P^2\) term anywhere. So cannot match.
- No match.

47) Has extra \(P c7\sin(c8 t+c9)\); must set \(c7=0\). Then matches.
- Matches GT.

48) Has extra \(P c6\sin(\cdot)\); must set \(c6=0\). Then matches.
- Matches GT.

49) Has \(P c5\sin(\cdot)\); must set \(c5=0\). Then matches.
- Matches GT.

- Matches GT.

- Then it lacks a \(P^2\) term entirely. So cannot match.
- No match.
